<p><b><a href="/wiki/List_of_Maccabi_sports_clubs_and_organisations" title="List of Maccabi sports clubs and organisations">Maccabi</a> Tel Aviv Football Club</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="he" xml:lang="he">מועדון כדורגל מכבי תל אביב</span>‎‎; <i>Moadon Kaduregel Maccabi Tel Aviv</i>) is an Israeli <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club and part of the <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv" title="Maccabi Tel Aviv">Maccabi Tel Aviv sports club</a>.</p>
<p>Founded in 1906<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_in_UEFA_Website_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_in_UEFA_Website-1">[1]</a></sup> as the HaRishon Le Zion-Yafo Association, Maccabi Tel Aviv is the oldest, largest and most decorated football club in Israel. With the establishment of the city of <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> in 1909, the club changed its name to Maccabi Tel Aviv. In 1922 they became the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> football club to participate in local competitions. The meaning of the name Maccabi – 'there is no one like you among the gods' (it refers to the Jewish god) – forms an integral part of the character of the team, which took the <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">Star of David</a> as their logo to represent the Jewish people. Maccabi Tel Aviv have won more titles than any other Israeli club, winning 22 <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Premier_League" title="Israeli Premier League">League Championships</a> (17 after Israeli independence), 23 prestigious <a href="/wiki/Israel_State_Cup" title="Israel State Cup">State Cups</a> (16 after Israeli independence), two <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League Cups</a> and an additional five <a href="/wiki/Toto_Cup" title="Toto Cup">Toto (League) Cups</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maccabi Tel Aviv is the only Israeli football team that have never been relegated from the Israeli Premier League and one of three only Israeli teams ever to make it to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> group stage. The club is named after the <a href="/wiki/Maccabees" title="Maccabees">Maccabees</a>.</p>
<p>Maccabi Tel Aviv FC invest a lot of money in the development and nurturing of young talent. The club's youth system operate football academies at three sites in the Tel Aviv area, working with over 750 children aged 6–15. The club also runs 17 youth teams with 400 players between 9 and 19 years old. These teams tend to compete very successfully in local and national leagues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Youth_Teams_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Youth_Teams-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-independence">Pre-independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1756" data-file-width="2394" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg/230px-Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg/345px-Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg/460px-Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_football_team_1939.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maccabi Tel Aviv in Australia, 1939</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="600" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg/150px-Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg/225px-Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg/300px-Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_1913.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maccabi Tel Aviv, 1913</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Durims decided to establish the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_League" title="Palestine League">Palestine League</a>. In the same year the <a href="/wiki/Israel_State_Cup" title="Israel State Cup">State Cup</a> was founded under the name "People Cup". That same year, the first <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv_derby" title="Tel Aviv derby">Tel Aviv derby</a> was played, with Maccabi winning, 3–0. Maccabi won their first State Cup in <a href="/wiki/1929_Palestine_Cup" title="1929 Palestine Cup">1929</a> after beating <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Jerusalem_F.C." title="Maccabi Jerusalem F.C.">Maccabi HaShmonai</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_first_years_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_first_years-4">[4]</a></sup> Maccabi won the State Cup for a second time in <a href="/wiki/1930_Palestine_Cup" title="1930 Palestine Cup">1930</a>, beating the <a href="/wiki/48th_(Northamptonshire)_Regiment_of_Foot" title="48th (Northamptonshire) Regiment of Foot">48th (Northamptonshire) Regiment of Foot</a> 2–1, and a third in <a href="/wiki/1933_Palestine_Cup" title="1933 Palestine Cup">1933</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Hapoel Tel Aviv F.C.">Hapoel Tel Aviv</a> were beaten, 1–0.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1942" data-file-width="1157" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg/150px-Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg/225px-Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg/300px-Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shmuel_ginzburg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Shmuel Ginzburg played for Maccabi Tel Aviv from 1936 to 1943 and contributed to the team's cup win in <a href="/wiki/1941_Palestine_Cup" title="1941 Palestine Cup">1941</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1936 the club was invited to play in the United States. On their way, Maccabi played in France, losing, 2–0, to <a href="/wiki/Racing_Club_de_France_football_Colombes_92" title="Racing Club de France football Colombes 92">Racing Paris</a> and 3–1 to <a href="/wiki/Lille_OSC" title="Lille OSC">Lille</a>. <a href="/wiki/1936%E2%80%9337_in_Mandatory_Palestine_football#Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_Tour_of_North_America" title="1936–37 in Mandatory Palestine football">In the United States</a>, Maccabi defeated the All-star team of New York City in front of 50,000 in <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_first_years_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_first_years-4">[4]</a></sup> Maccabi also defeated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Soccer_League_(1933-1983)" title="American Soccer League (1933-1983)">American Soccer League</a> team in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> on their home ground, 1–0, and also played in Canada, where they drew, 1–1, with <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> All-Stars. Maccabi continued their tour in the USA and lost, 3–2, to <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Stars_(soccer)" title="St. Louis Stars (soccer)">St. Louis Stars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> Celtics.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="592" data-file-width="1169" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg/230px-%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg/345px-%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg/460px-%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D7%9E%D7%9B%D7%91%D7%99_%D7%AA%D7%9C_%D7%90%D7%91%D7%99%D7%91_1921.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maccabi Tel Aviv, 1921</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After returning from the United States, Maccabi players went on strike because they had not been paid. In 1937, after a year of strike action, the Football Association accepted their demands and the team ended their strike. In that year, Maccabi Tel Aviv also won their first league title. In 1939, after the start of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Maccabi won their second championship. At the end of the season, Maccabi went to <a href="/wiki/1938%E2%80%9339_in_Mandatory_Palestine_football#Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_Tour_of_Australia" title="1938–39 in Mandatory Palestine football">another tour</a>, this time to Australia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_first_years_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-The_first_years-4">[4]</a></sup> where they were advertised as the "<a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>" team and occasionally the Maccabi Palestine team. They played 18 games, winning 11, losing 5 and drawing 2. The games were against State sides (<a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, Victoria, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, South Australia and Western Australia), regional sides and five "tests" against the <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australian national team</a>, winning one, drawing one and losing three.</p>
<p>In 1941 Maccabi won their first "<a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_first_years_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-The_first_years-4">[4]</a></sup> Winning both the league and State Cup, beating Hapoel Tel Aviv, 2–1, in the final. Between 1941 and 1945 the league was suspended because of the war, but Maccabi continued playing friendly matches. In 1946, the league was still suspended but the State Cup returned with Maccabi beating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hapoel_Ironi_Rishon_LeZion_F.C." title="Hapoel Ironi Rishon LeZion F.C.">Hapoel Rishon LeZion</a>, 6–0, on aggregate in the final. In 1947 the league resumed, and Maccabi won it, and also reached the cup final. In the match against <a href="/wiki/Beitar_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Beitar Tel Aviv F.C.">Beitar Tel Aviv</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Hatikva_Neighborhood_Stadium" title="Hatikva Neighborhood Stadium">Hatikva Neighborhood Stadium</a> Maccabi were winning, 3–2, when the referee disallowed a goal by Beitar. The Beitar players and their supporters stormed at the referee and Yom-Tov Mansherov, defender of Beitar Tel Aviv, snapped the Cup. As a result, the referee ended the game and Maccabi were awarded a technical victory, thus winning a second double. Forty-five years later the cup was found in <a href="/wiki/Petah_Tikva" title="Petah Tikva">Petah Tikva</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s">1950s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1950s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:217px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Makabi46.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="798" data-file-width="1119" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Makabi46.jpg/215px-Makabi46.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Makabi46.jpg/323px-Makabi46.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Makabi46.jpg/430px-Makabi46.jpg 2x" width="215"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Makabi46.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maccabi team after winning the <a href="/wiki/1946_Palestine_Cup" title="1946 Palestine Cup">1946 State Cup</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Israel_cup_1957.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1367" data-file-width="800" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Israel_cup_1957.jpg/180px-Israel_cup_1957.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Israel_cup_1957.jpg/270px-Israel_cup_1957.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Israel_cup_1957.jpg/360px-Israel_cup_1957.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Israel_cup_1957.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Noach Reznik with the State Cup, 1957.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This decade is considered Maccabi Tel Aviv's "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Age" title="Golden Age">Golden Age</a>", in which they won five championships and four <a href="/wiki/Israel_Football_Association" title="Israel Football Association">Israel Football Association</a> Cups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> The "Golden Age" actually began with the establishment of the State of Israel, with Maccabi Tel Aviv winning the league title in the 1949–50 season. The deciding match of the season was the second <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv_derby" title="Tel Aviv derby">Tel Aviv derby</a> against <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Hapoel Tel Aviv F.C.">Hapoel Tel Aviv</a>, which Maccabi won, 1–0, thanks to a goal from striker <a href="/wiki/Yosef_Merimovich" title="Yosef Merimovich">Yosef "Yosale" Merimovich</a> that sealed Maccabi Tel Aviv's first post-independence championship title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_50.27s_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_50.27s-5">[5]</a></sup> Merimovich was just one member of a squad of outstanding players that left Maccabi Tel Aviv unchallenged in their domination of the Israeli Premier League during the 1950s. That squad included the likes of defenders <a href="/wiki/Itzhak_Schneor" title="Itzhak Schneor">Itzhak Schneor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eli_Fuchs" title="Eli Fuchs">Eli Fuchs</a>, goalkeeper Avraham Bandouri, striker <a href="/wiki/Zvi_Studinski" title="Zvi Studinski">Zvi Studinski</a> and of course the club's legendary centre forward <a href="/wiki/Yehoshua_Glazer" title="Yehoshua Glazer">Yehoshua "Shiye" Glazer</a>. Glazer, who won the top scorer title in 1952 with 27 goals, is considered Maccabi Tel Aviv's greatest ever striker and was the Club's highest goal scorer until <a href="/wiki/Avi_Nimni" title="Avi Nimni">Avi Nimni</a> broke his record in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_Scorers_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Scorers-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Itzhak_Schneor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="743" data-file-width="449" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Itzhak_Schneor.jpg/110px-Itzhak_Schneor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Itzhak_Schneor.jpg/165px-Itzhak_Schneor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Itzhak_Schneor.jpg/220px-Itzhak_Schneor.jpg 2x" width="110"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Itzhak_Schneor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Itzhak_Schneor" title="Itzhak Schneor">Itzhak Schneor</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 1951–52 season was Maccabi's second league title after the establishment of the State, which they won by eight points ahead of <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Petah_Tikva_F.C." title="Maccabi Petah Tikva F.C.">Maccabi Petah Tikva</a>, though they lost the IFA Cup final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_50.27s_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_50.27s-5">[5]</a></sup> That loss only inspired them to win an historic first double in the 1953–54 season, once again winning the league ahead of Maccabi Petah Tikva. That year's Cup final provided them with the opportunity to put in one of their most devastating performances, crushing their opponents <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Netanya_F.C." title="Maccabi Netanya F.C.">Maccabi Netanya</a>, 4–0, with a brace from Glazer and individual goals from Studinski and midfielder <a href="/wiki/Israel_Halivner" title="Israel Halivner">Israel Halivner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_50.27s_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-The_50.27s-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was the following season that the great <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Petah_Tikva_F.C." title="Hapoel Petah Tikva F.C.">Hapoel Petah Tikva</a> team of midfielder <a href="/wiki/Nahum_Stelmach" title="Nahum Stelmach">Nahum Stelmach</a> and associates burst on the scene and captured the championship from Maccabi Tel Aviv after a down to the wire finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_50.27s_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-The_50.27s-5">[5]</a></sup> Still Maccabi Tel Aviv weren't prepared to surrender all the titles that season and came up trumps in a 3–1 victory over the same Hapoel Petah Tikva in the IFA Cup final. Maccabi went on to beat them to the title in two more seasons, 1955–56 and 1957–58, completing their fifth National Championship in the first decade of the modern state of Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_50.27s_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-The_50.27s-5">[5]</a></sup> That final season title was complemented by a double, with Maccabi beating <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Haifa_F.C." title="Hapoel Haifa F.C.">Hapoel Haifa</a> in the IFA Cup final, 2–0.</p>
<p>The following season Maccabi Tel Aviv won their second consecutive IFA Cup in a final that will be remembered as one of the most famous in the entire history of the competition. Maccabi appeared to be cruising to victory with a seemingly unassailable 4–0 lead just ten minutes from time. But within five of those final ten minutes Hapoel Petah Tikva pulled back three of those goals, guaranteeing one of the most exciting finales in IFA Cup history. But in the end Maccabi held on to celebrate yet another IFA Cup triumph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_50.27s_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-The_50.27s-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MaccabiTAOLD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="463" data-file-width="500" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2d/MaccabiTAOLD.jpg/225px-MaccabiTAOLD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2d/MaccabiTAOLD.jpg/338px-MaccabiTAOLD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2d/MaccabiTAOLD.jpg/450px-MaccabiTAOLD.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MaccabiTAOLD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Maccabi Tel Aviv's original logo.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_(GPO)_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg/300px-Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg/450px-Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg/600px-Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_%28GPO%29_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_(GPO)_-_Hapoel_Haifa_Goalie.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
State Cup final, 1964, <a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_Stadium" title="Bloomfield Stadium">Bloomfield Stadium</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the "Golden Years" of the 1950s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_50.27s_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-The_50.27s-5">[5]</a></sup> Maccabi Tel Aviv found themselves as the new decade began challenged and ultimately eclipsed by the emergent HaPoel Petach Tikva, who during the late 1950s and early 1960s won five consecutive league titles. The second of those championships, in 1960, came at Maccabi's expense, with the Yellows leading the table on the last day of the season only to disappointingly lose their final match to Hapoel Haifa thereby handing the championship to Hapoel Petah Tikva.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_60.27s_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_60.27s-7">[7]</a></sup> The outstanding player of Maccabi's season had been <a href="/wiki/Rafi_Levi" title="Rafi Levi">Rafi Levi</a>, one of the greatest strikers in the club's history, who was the league's leading goal scorer with 19 goals. A year later the Brazilian club <a href="/wiki/Santos_FC" title="Santos FC">Santos</a> visited Israel,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_60.27s_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_60.27s-7">[7]</a></sup> along with their legendary player, <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a>, for a friendly match against a side composed of the best players from both Maccabi Tel Aviv and Hapoel Petah Tikva. But even the combined forces of the two best clubs in the country were no match for the Brazilians, who won, 3–1.</p>
<p>After a number of unremarkable seasons, the 1960s saw the return of Maccabi Tel Aviv with one of their greatest coaches, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Beit_haLevi" title="Jerry Beit haLevi">Jerry Beit haLevi</a>, who had served the club as a player in the 1930s and, with the exception of one year, managed the club for the ten years between 1947 and 1957.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerry_Bet_Halevi_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jerry_Bet_Halevi-8">[8]</a></sup> Under his guardianship Maccabi Tel Aviv slowly returned to form and in the 1963–64 season won the Israel Football Association Cup after a second replay against Hapoel Haifa, which Maccabi won, 2–1. The following season Maccabi Tel Aviv repeated the feat by exactly the same score, this time in a dramatic extra time victory over <a href="/wiki/Bnei_Yehuda_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Bnei Yehuda Tel Aviv F.C.">Bnei Yehuda</a> that included goals by midfielders Moshe Asis and Rafi Baranes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_60.27s_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-The_60.27s-7">[7]</a></sup> In the 1966–67 season Maccabi added a third IFA Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> This time the opponent in the final were city rivals Hapoel Tel Aviv whom Maccabi defeated by the very same 2–1 score line, with goals from midfielder Uri Kedmi and striker <a href="/wiki/Rachamim_Talbi" title="Rachamim Talbi">Rachamim Talbi</a>.</p>
<p>While the Cup competition was held as scheduled that year, the league was interrupted by the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> and was extended into 1968. Now coached by Israel Halivner, Maccabi Tel Aviv won their first and only championship of the decade after a combined 60 match weeks, leading Hapoel Petah Tikva by three points at the top of the Israel Premier League table. But by far the most memorable event of the decade was Maccabi's success in the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> in 1969,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> the first Israeli football club to win an international competition in the country's history. Now managed by former striking great Yossele Merimovich, Maccabi beat <a href="/wiki/South_Korean" title="South Korean">South Korean</a> side <a href="/wiki/Yangzee_FC" title="Yangzee FC">Yangzee FC</a> in extra time through a goal by striker Dror Bar Nur.</p>
<p>A less successful decade for Maccabi Tel Aviv perhaps, but the club still managed to win one championship and three Israel Football Association Cups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> Among the great names of the decade were midfielder Nissim Bachar, defender Meir Nimni, defender <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Bello" title="Menachem Bello">Menachem "Miko" Bello</a>, defender <a href="/wiki/Zvi_Rosen" title="Zvi Rosen">Tzvika Rosen</a>, goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Haim_Levin" title="Haim Levin">Haim Levin</a>, midfielder Moshe Asis, striker Rafi Levi and midfielder <a href="/wiki/Giora_Spiegel" title="Giora Spiegel">Giora Spiegel</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MikiBello.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1104" data-file-width="900" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/MikiBello.jpg/240px-MikiBello.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/MikiBello.jpg/360px-MikiBello.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/MikiBello.jpg/480px-MikiBello.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MikiBello.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
All-time most capped player, <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Bello" title="Menachem Bello">Menachem Bello</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Beit_haLevi_1939.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="299" data-file-width="258" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Jerry_Beit_haLevi_1939.jpg/180px-Jerry_Beit_haLevi_1939.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/05/Jerry_Beit_haLevi_1939.jpg 1.5x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jerry_Beit_haLevi_1939.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jerry_Beit_haLevi" title="Jerry Beit haLevi">Jerry Beit haLevi</a>, won 10 championships and 8 state cups with Maccabi as a player, coach and chairman.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By Maccabi Tel Aviv standards, the 1960s had not been a particularly successful decade. With the coming of the 1970s, all that was about to change. The very first year of the decade was a stellar indication of that change as the team, under the able leadership of the late <a href="/wiki/David_Schweitzer" title="David Schweitzer">David Schweitzer</a>, won an historic double.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> The Israeli Football Association (IFA) Cup final was won with a 2–1 victory over Maccabi Netanya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_70.27s_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_70.27s-9">[9]</a></sup> The league title on the other hand was ensured only on goal difference, but one that was built in part upon one of the finest performances in the club's history, a 5–0 thrashing of city rivals Hapoel Tel Aviv in the Tel Aviv derby. On a rainy day at the end of January 1970, 20,000 spectators saw Maccabi midfielder Giora Shpiegel score a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> to lead his side to an unforgettable victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_70.27s_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_70.27s-9">[9]</a></sup> But despite that defeat, Hapoel stayed neck-and-neck with Maccabi until the very last week and it was Hapoel who found themselves in second place on goal difference when the season reached its conclusion.</p>
<p>The following season was a weak one for Maccabi Tel Aviv that saw them finish tenth in the league table.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_70.27s_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-The_70.27s-9">[9]</a></sup> But just one year later they were fully back on track winning their second championship of the decade in the 1971–72 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> One of the stars of that season, and one of the greatest strikers in the club's history, was Dror Bar Nur, who scored 16 of the club's 45 goals in the league and added two more in other competitions.</p>
<p>Just four years later Maccabi Tel Aviv found themselves for the first time in a relegation battle, with the final week of the 1975–76 season seeing no less than nine clubs battling it out to stay in the upper tier. Maccabi beat <a href="/wiki/Beitar_Jerusalem_F.C." title="Beitar Jerusalem F.C.">Beitar Jerusalem</a>, 2–0, with goals from strikers Rachamim Talbi and <a href="/wiki/Benny_Tabak" title="Benny Tabak">Benny Tabak</a>, thus escaping what would have been the first drop in the club's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_70.27s_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-The_70.27s-9">[9]</a></sup> In April of that same year, leaders of the English <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Football League First Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>, arrived in Israel for a friendly to face a Maccabi Tel Aviv side bolstered by three of the Israeli Premier League's brightest stars of the time: Maccabi Netanya strikers <a href="/wiki/Mordechai_Spiegler" title="Mordechai Spiegler">Mordechai "Motaleh" Spiegler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oded_Machnes" title="Oded Machnes">Oded Machnes</a> and Beitar Jerusalem midfielder <a href="/wiki/Uri_Malmilian" title="Uri Malmilian">Uri Malmilian</a>. Maccabi won the match, 2–1, with goals from Malmilian and Spiegler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_70.27s_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-The_70.27s-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>A year later and once again Maccabi Tel Aviv went from near disaster to the league summit, securing in the 1976/77 season their second double of the decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> They won the title three points ahead of <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Jaffa_F.C." title="Maccabi Jaffa F.C.">Maccabi Jaffa</a> and with 47 goals, the highest number in the league. Striker <a href="/wiki/Vicky_Peretz" title="Vicky Peretz">Vicky Peretz</a> finished as the league's leading goal scorer with 17 league goals and another five in IFA Cup competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_70.27s_9-5"><a href="#cite_note-The_70.27s-9">[9]</a></sup> But it was Benny Tabak's lone goal against Beitar Tel Aviv in front of 30,000 spectators at <a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_Stadium" title="Bloomfield Stadium">Bloomfield Stadium</a> that earned Maccabi the IFA Cup and their second double in the space of seven years.</p>
<p>Among the great Maccabi players of the time were strikers Benny Tabak and Vicky Peretz and the late <a href="/wiki/Avi_Cohen" title="Avi Cohen">Avi Cohen</a>, who earned the nickname "Libero" (from the Italian, a fullback who is given freedom – libero – to roam from his position to play a role in offence as well) and is thought to be one of the greatest defenders in the history of Israeli football. One of his most memorable goals was in a 2–0 derby victory over Hapoel Tel Aviv in 1978, when the defender struck an absolutely unstoppable ball from the edge of the area straight into the opposition net.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_70.27s_9-6"><a href="#cite_note-The_70.27s-9">[9]</a></sup> Vicky Peretz and Benny Tabak are remembered as two of the greatest strikers in the history of the club, with the former scoring 67 and the latter 121 goals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_Scorers_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Scorers-6">[6]</a></sup> in the yellow and blue jersey of Maccabi Tel Aviv.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2650" data-file-width="3071" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg/230px-Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg/345px-Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg/460px-Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reuven_Rivlin_with_Bonni_Ginzburg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Oded_Machnes" title="Oded Machnes">Oded Machnes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bonni_Ginzburg" title="Bonni Ginzburg">Bonni Ginzburg</a> (from left to right), both played for Maccabi in the 80's.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 1980s saw a period of below par achievements for Maccabi Tel Aviv FC, earning the decade the nickname the "thin years". While adding two Israel Football Association (IFA) Cups to the trophy cabinet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-8"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> the club remained without a league title throughout the decade. The first of the two consecutive IFA Cup triumphs, however, was won in dramatic fashion in a final against <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Haifa_F.C." title="Maccabi Haifa F.C.">Maccabi Haifa</a> in the 1986–87 season. While Maccabi Tel Aviv, third in the table, finished six places above their northern namesakes, the Cup final was a tight affair that ended, 3–3, after extra time and was decided in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out" title="Penalty shoot-out">penalty shoot-out</a>. And it was striker Benny Tabak's final kick that saw Maccabi Tel Aviv lift their first IFA Cup in ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_80.27s_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_80.27s-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following season Maccabi Tel Aviv, now under the stewardship of Giora Spiegel,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GIORA_SPIEGEL_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-GIORA_SPIEGEL-11">[11]</a></sup> underwent their worst defeat in the club's history, a 0–10 rout suffered at the hands of that same Maccabi Haifa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_80.27s_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_80.27s-10">[10]</a></sup> Yet only three weeks later the club appeared in their second consecutive intriguing IFA Cup final, this time against their arch big city rivals Hapoel Tel Aviv. Despite the fresh memories of their lacklustre performance in Haifa the team succeeded in returning to form thanks to a wonderful goal by midfielder Mickey Cohen and yet another from Benny Tabak that led to a 2–1 victory and a second straight IFA Cup title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_80.27s_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-The_80.27s-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another memorable event of the 1980s occurred at the beginning of the decade, in a match against Beitar Jerusalem held at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/YMCA_Stadium" title="YMCA Stadium">YMCA Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> in the second matchweek of the 1981–82 season. The match referee <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Klein_(referee)" title="Abraham Klein (referee)">Avraham Klein</a>, of international reputation, disallowed a Beitar goal but the players continued to celebrate. Maccabi defender Menahem "Miko" Belo quickly resumed play, passed on to midfielder <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moti_Ivanir" title="Moti Ivanir">Moti Ivanir</a> who found himself facing the Beitar keeper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yossi_Mizrachi" title="Yossi Mizrachi">Yossi Mizrachi</a> on his own. To the great ire of the local fans he scored the goal that would ultimately lead to a 1–2 Maccabi victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_80.27s_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-The_80.27s-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the less than scintillating nature of Maccabi's performances throughout the decade, the club was blessed with a number of outstanding players, including Moti Ivanir, midfielder Alon Natan, goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Bonni_Ginzburg" title="Bonni Ginzburg">Bonni Ginzburg</a> and striker <a href="/wiki/Eli_Driks" title="Eli Driks">Eli Driks</a> who succeeded in leaving their mark on the club's history. Ivanir, who made his maiden performance for Maccabi aged 16, scored 67 times playing for the club throughout the decade, with the exception of the two years he spent at Dutch side <a href="/wiki/Roda_JC_Kerkrade" title="Roda JC Kerkrade">Roda JC Kerkrade</a>. Alon Natan found the net 40 times before leaving the club for Bnei Yehuda at the end of the 1989–90 season. He was subsequently forced into retirement at age 23 due to injury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_80.27s_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-The_80.27s-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bonni Ginzburg protected the Maccabi goal from the beginning of the decade until the 1987–88 season. He earned himself a place on the <a href="/wiki/Israel_national_football_team" title="Israel national football team">national squad</a> and two years later became the first Israeli goalkeeper to play abroad. Eli Driks, one of the club's all-time greatest strikers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_Scorers_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Scorers-6">[6]</a></sup> came through the youth ranks at the beginning of the 1980s and began a successful career at the fulcrum of the Maccabi Tel Aviv attack that lasted 20 years.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avi_Nimni_new.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="331" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Avi_Nimni_new.jpg/170px-Avi_Nimni_new.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Avi_Nimni_new.jpg/255px-Avi_Nimni_new.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6a/Avi_Nimni_new.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avi_Nimni_new.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Avi_Nimni" title="Avi Nimni">Avi Nimni</a>, Maccabi's greatest player of the 90's.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the considerably less than spectacular decade of the 1980s, a young head coach by the name of <a href="/wiki/Avram_Grant" title="Avram Grant">Avram Grant</a> took over the reins at Maccabi Tel Aviv and brought with him a whole slew of young players that together brought about one of the most successful decades in the club's history. By the time the decade had reached its halfway point the team had already won an historic "double" along with two more championships, two State Cups and one <a href="/wiki/Toto_Cup" title="Toto Cup">Toto (League) Cup</a>, to which two more would be added before the decade had drawn to a close.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-9"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> Within a matter of a few short years, the glow surrounding Maccabi Tel Aviv, which had dimmed somewhat in the 80's, had returned and once again the yellow and blue of Maccabi became the national colours of Israel's football culture.</p>
<p>It all started in the 1991–92 season, when by virtue of exceptional talent and quality attacking football under the leadership of Avraham Grant, Maccabi Tel Aviv won the league championship for the first time in thirteen years. What contributed to this talent was, among other things, the arrival at the club of the Russian national goalkeeper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Ubarov" title="Alexander Ubarov">Alexander Ubarov</a>, who in time became a real Maccabi Tel Aviv legend. With him arrived defender <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Polukarov" title="Alexander Polukarov">Alexander Polukarov</a>, who also left an enduring mark at the club and together with midfielder Uri Malmilyan and the young midfielders Avi Nimni and <a href="/wiki/Itzik_Zohar" title="Itzik Zohar">Itzik Zohar</a> returned Maccabi Tel Aviv to the top of Israeli football. In the 1992–93 season, after winning the Toto (League) Cup, this talented and successful group of young players of the 90's got their first taste of victory in the prestigious State Cup after goals by Itsik Zohar and fellow midfielder <a href="/wiki/Nir_Klinger" title="Nir Klinger">Nir Klinger</a> decided the final against arch rivals Hapoel Tel Aviv. But despite finishing an excellent season with 88 points, the league title, and hence an historic "double", remained beyond their grasp as Maccabi Haifa enjoyed a spectacular season that saw them play all 39 league matches without a loss and pip Maccabi Tel Aviv to the championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_90.27s_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_90.27s-12">[12]</a></sup> But the following season Grant and his charges compensated for their disappointment when defender <a href="/wiki/Alon_Brumer" title="Alon Brumer">Alon Brumer</a>'s famous goal in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beer_Sheva" title="Beer Sheva">Beer Sheva</a> succeeded in returning the championship to Maccabi Tel Aviv in dramatic fashion.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avram_Grant_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1894" data-file-width="2851" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Avram_Grant_2012.jpg/210px-Avram_Grant_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Avram_Grant_2012.jpg/315px-Avram_Grant_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Avram_Grant_2012.jpg/420px-Avram_Grant_2012.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avram_Grant_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Avram_Grant" title="Avram Grant">Avram Grant</a>, Head coach, 1991–95, 1996–00.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the end of the 1995 season the "Mofet" Group took control of Maccabi Tel Aviv and as a result of Avraham Grant's decision to leave the club, a new coach, <a href="/wiki/Dror_Kashtan" title="Dror Kashtan">Dror Kashtan</a>, took over the reins for what would prove to be one of the best seasons in the club's history. Their chief rivals were once again Maccabi Haifa, and the team traveled to their <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Eliezer_Stadium" title="Kiryat Eliezer Stadium">Kiryat Eliezer Stadium</a> for what will always be remembered as the must-win match of that season. As the players headed for the dressing room trailing 1–0 at half time, coach Kashtan controversially decided to return his players to await their Maccabi Haifa rivals on the pitch. In the second half, goals by striker Eli Dricks and midfielders Nir Klinger and Avi Nimni turned the match around, and that 1–3 victory not only handed Maccabi Tel Aviv the championship but also paved the way for the "double" after a 4–1 thrashing of <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Rishon_LeZion_F.C." title="Hapoel Rishon LeZion F.C.">Hapoel Rishon Lezion</a> in the State Cup final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_90.27s_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_90.27s-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>With Israel's entrance into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_football" title="European football">European football</a> in 1992,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Israel_Football_Association_on_UEFA_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Israel_Football_Association_on_UEFA-13">[13]</a></sup> Maccabi Tel Aviv also turned their attention to leaving their mark in this prestigious competition as well. The 1992–93 season marked the first time Maccabi Tel Aviv competed in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> qualifiers and in the first round they defeated the Maltese club <a href="/wiki/Valletta_F.C." title="Valletta F.C.">Valletta</a> but lost to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian" title="Belgian">Belgian</a> side <a href="/wiki/Club_Brugge_KV" title="Club Brugge KV">Club Brugge</a> in the second round. In the 1994–95 season, Maccabi were knocked out in the second round of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> by German side <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a> on a 2–0 aggregate. The following season Maccabi once again tried their luck in the Champions League qualifiers and almost succeeded, but a 2–1 aggregate loss to the <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Swiss</a> club <a href="/wiki/Grasshopper_Club_Z%C3%BCrich" title="Grasshopper Club Zürich">Grasshoppers</a> handed the latter the keys to the group stages. In 1996 it was the powerful Turkish side <a href="/wiki/Fenerbah%C3%A7e_S.K._(football)" title="Fenerbahçe S.K. (football)">Fenerbahçe</a> that stood between Maccabi and the group stages and in the resultant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> competition they encountered, and subsequently lost to, the Spanish club <a href="/wiki/CD_Tenerife" title="CD Tenerife">Tenerife</a>. In the 1999–00 season, Maccabi got past Lithuanian opponents <a href="/wiki/FBK_Kaunas" title="FBK Kaunas">FBK Kaunas</a> in the UEFA Cup qualifiers but then lost to French competitors <a href="/wiki/RC_Lens" title="RC Lens">Lens</a> 4–3 on aggregate in round one.</p>
<p>In the 1990s Maccabi Tel Aviv were blessed with many talented players, among them defenders <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amir_Shelach" title="Amir Shelach">Amir Shelach</a> and the Brumer brothers <a href="/wiki/Gadi_Brumer" title="Gadi Brumer">Gadi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alon_Brumer" title="Alon Brumer">Alon</a>, midfielder <a href="/wiki/Noam_Shoham" title="Noam Shoham">Noam Shoham</a> and strikers Meir Melika and <a href="/wiki/Nir_Sivilia" title="Nir Sivilia">Nir Sivilia</a>. Leading the team into battle was the genius of captain Nir Klinger, the free-kick artistry of Itzik Zohar and perhaps the greatest player in Maccabi Tel Aviv's history, midfielder <a href="/wiki/Avi_Nimni" title="Avi Nimni">Avi Nimni</a>. In 1997 the "Mofet" Group broke up and the club was taken over by Loni Herzikovich.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yeini.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="592" data-file-width="531" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Yeini.JPG/200px-Yeini.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Yeini.JPG/300px-Yeini.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Yeini.JPG/400px-Yeini.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yeini.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sheran_Yeini" title="Sheran Yeini">Sheran Yeini</a>, played 11 years in the club and was captain of the team.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With a particularly attacking style of football promoted by head coach Nir Klinger, the second millennium got off to a very good start for Maccabi Tel Aviv, who won two consecutive coveted State Cups. The first came in the 2000–01 season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maccabi_titles_2-10"><a href="#cite_note-Maccabi_titles-2">[2]</a></sup> one that saw Maccabi finish just fourth in the table but with the highest number of goals of any club in the Israeli Premier League, 71. Particularly memorable was Maccabi's 7–0 demolition of Beitar Jerusalem towards the end of the season and the jaw-dropping total of 10 goals to just one reply against Hapoel Rishon Lezion in January of that same year. It was that exceptional attacking prowess that resulted in Maccabi's receiving the State Cup from the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Israel" title="President of Israel">country's president</a> after a 3–0 victory over Maccabi Petah Tikva in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Millennium_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Millennium-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following season will largely be remembered for the tragic event that occurred on 26 January 2002 during a match against Beitar Jerusalem. Without a preceding incident, Maccabi defender <a href="/wiki/Meni_Levi" title="Meni Levi">Meni Levi</a> suddenly collapsed in the middle of the pitch, picked himself up and then collapsed again. He received treatment on the pitch for quite a long time before being rushed to a hospital. The game, in the meantime, was not resumed. For a number of years Levi received treatment at the rehabilitation facility Beit Levinstein in <a href="/wiki/Ra%27anana" title="Ra'anana">Ra'anana</a> but unfortunately was unable to recover and was returned to his family. Subsequently the club decided to retire Levi's number twelve jersey entirely. As the year progressed the team succeeded in recovering from this tragic incident and ended the season with their second State Cup title in as many years. In the final, Maccabi Tel Aviv won a penalty shoot-out against that season's champion, Maccabi Haifa, after extra time saw the two sides locked in a goalless draw.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="656" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg/300px-Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg/450px-Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg/600px-Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maccabi_Tel-Aviv_against_Dynamo_Kiev2.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Team photo taken before a match against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dynamo_Kyiv" title="Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The following season Maccabi Tel Aviv won a dramatic league championship from title rivals Maccabi Haifa. On the eve of the last day of the season, head coach Nir Klinger's lads led the league table on goal difference alone. On the day itself Maccabi Haifa led 0–5 at half time against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.C._Ironi_Ashdod" title="F.C. Ironi Ashdod">Ashdod</a> while Maccabi were still looking for their first goal against Hapoel Petah Tikva. Only in the second half did they score the three goals (to no reply) that pushed their goal difference past Maccabi Haifa and brought the Championship plate back to the Maccabi Tel Aviv trophy cabinet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Millennium_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Millennium-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maccabi's most significant achievement of the decade came in the 2004–05 season when the team reached the group stages of the Champions League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Group_D_04.2F05_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Group_D_04.2F05-15">[15]</a></sup> In the play-off stages they beat the Greek side <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PAOK_F.C." title="PAOK F.C.">PAOK Thessaloniki</a> and became Israel's second club, after Maccabi Haifa two years earlier, to reach the group stages. There they were drawn against three giants of European football, the German <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>, the Italian <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> and the Dutch <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>. Nonetheless Maccabi succeeded in finishing the group stage with a precious four points after beating Ajax and drawing with Juventus at home. Paradoxically they ended an unstable league season eighth in the table but once again came away with the State Cup after winning a penalty shoot-out in a final against <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Herzliya_F.C." title="Maccabi Herzliya F.C.">Maccabi Herzliya</a> that ended 2–2 after extra time.</p>
<p>After this third State Cup in five seasons, Maccabi's fortunes dipped drastically and other clubs took turns winning the league and the Cup. The 2005–06 season will be remembered in particular, earning the nickname "the Galacticos season", for a team that brought together the likes of Israeli international <a href="/wiki/Eyal_Berkovic" title="Eyal Berkovic">Eyal Berkovic</a>, Croatian star <a href="/wiki/%C4%90ovani_Roso" title="Đovani Roso">Đovani Roso</a> and Maccabi all-time great <a href="/wiki/Avi_Nimni" title="Avi Nimni">Avi Nimni</a>. Despite the star-studded squad, Maccabi failed to translate that quality into winning form and ended the season in the bottom half of the table. In the 2010–11 season Maccabi enjoyed one moment of glory in Europe, beating a strong Greek <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiacos</a> side 1–0 in the home leg of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> qualifiers. The victory sent Maccabi into the first round of the competition where, despite an exciting 4–3 victory in the home leg, Maccabi failed to surpass French giants <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a> after a 2–0 loss in the French capital. The following season Maccabi claimed a famous victory against Greek side <a href="/wiki/Panathinaikos_F.C." title="Panathinaikos F.C.">Panathinaikos</a>, beating them 3–0 at Bloomfield Stadium in the qualifying stages of the Europa League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Group_E_11.2F12_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Group_E_11.2F12-16">[16]</a></sup> It was a year Maccabi actually did succeed in reaching the group stage of the competition but collected just two points in a group that contained Turkish side <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F_J.K." title="Beşiktaş J.K.">Beşiktaş</a>, the Ukrainians <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> and the English <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jordi_Cruyff_Era_.282012_and_beyond.29">Jordi Cruyff Era (2012 and beyond)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Jordi Cruyff Era (2012 and beyond)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DK-Maccabi_(4).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/DK-Maccabi_%284%29.jpg/250px-DK-Maccabi_%284%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/DK-Maccabi_%284%29.jpg/375px-DK-Maccabi_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/DK-Maccabi_%284%29.jpg/500px-DK-Maccabi_%284%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Paulo_Sousa" title="Paulo Sousa">Paulo Sousa</a>, Coach in 2013–14.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2012–13 season finally put an end to Maccabi Tel Aviv's bad fortunes in the league as they won their first championship in a decade. Under the stewardship of New Director of Football <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Cruyff" title="Jordi Cruyff">Jordi Cruyff</a> and Spanish head coach <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Garc%C3%ADa_Junyent" title="Óscar García Junyent">Óscar García</a>, Maccabi dominated the league and claimed the title by thirteen points ahead of their nearest rival. They finished the season with the league's highest goal total of 78 while conceding the fewest with just 30 goals conceded. Leading that attack was the league's highest goal scorer, striker <a href="/wiki/Eliran_Atar" title="Eliran Atar">Eliran Atar</a> with 22, but he was joined by midfielder <a href="/wiki/Maharan_Radi" title="Maharan Radi">Maharan Radi</a> with eight (plus eleven assists), young striker <a href="/wiki/Moanes_Dabour" title="Moanes Dabour">Moanes Dabour</a> with ten and Swedish striker <a href="/wiki/Rade_Prica" title="Rade Prica">Rade Prica</a> (eight) and midfielder <a href="/wiki/Eran_Zahavi" title="Eran Zahavi">Eran Zahavi</a> (seven) who both arrived at the club in the January transfer window. In defense the tone was set by Maccabi's two center halves, <a href="/wiki/Eitan_Tibi" title="Eitan Tibi">Eitan Tibi</a> and the Spaniard <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Garc%C3%ADa_Bad%C3%ADas" title="Carlos García Badías">Carlos García</a>, backed up by the excellence of Maccabi Tel Aviv's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nigerian" title="Nigerian">Nigerian</a> goalkeeper, <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Enyeama" title="Vincent Enyeama">Vincent Enyeama</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="652" data-file-width="570" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg/150px-ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg/225px-ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg/300px-ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ZahaviAfterScoringAgainstHapoel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eran_Zahavi" title="Eran Zahavi">Eran Zahavi</a>, 99 goals in 120 league apps for Maccabi</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2013–14 season saw a change in the club's Coach Position with <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Sousa" title="Paulo Sousa">Paulo Sousa</a> replacing Oscar Garcia, as well as several players leaving and new players arriving. Notably <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Enyeama" title="Vincent Enyeama">Vincent Enyeama</a> left for <a href="/wiki/Lille_OSC" title="Lille OSC">Lille</a> with Goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Colinas" title="Juan Pablo Colinas">Juan Pablo Colinas</a> joining between the posts, and <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Mitrovi%C4%87" title="Nikola Mitrović">Nikola Mitrović</a> joining from <a href="/wiki/Videoton_FC" title="Videoton FC">Videoton</a>. The team continued its success in the league and claimed another championship behind <a href="/wiki/Eran_Zahavi" title="Eran Zahavi">Eran Zahavi</a>'s goal scoring.The Team's main rivals this season were Hapoel Be'er Sheva who came in second. The team also enjoyed relative success in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> as they advanced to the round of 32 after a difficult group stage, before ultimately being ousted by <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">Basel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Group_F_13.2F14_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Group_F_13.2F14-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Bosz_crop.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="252" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Peter_Bosz_crop.png/150px-Peter_Bosz_crop.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Peter_Bosz_crop.png/225px-Peter_Bosz_crop.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Peter_Bosz_crop.png 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Bosz_crop.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Peter_Bosz" title="Peter Bosz">Peter Bosz</a>, Coached in 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2014–15 season was characterized by a difficult start. <a href="/wiki/2014_Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_conflict" title="2014 Israel–Gaza conflict">Operation Protective Edge</a> meant that the qualifying games to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> were held away from Israel, leading Maccabi to be ousted from both the Champions League and the Europa League. There was also a shake up at the coach position as <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Sousa" title="Paulo Sousa">Paulo Sousa</a> left for <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">Basel</a>. <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Garc%C3%ADa_Junyent" title="Óscar García Junyent">Óscar García</a> returned but left before the beginning of the season and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Pako_Ayestar%C3%A1n" title="Pako Ayestarán">Pako Ayestarán</a>. During the Tel Aviv Derby on 3 November 2014, a fan from Hapoel Tel Aviv broke onto the pitch with an intent to assault Maccabi Star <a href="/wiki/Eran_Zahavi" title="Eran Zahavi">Eran Zahavi</a> who was shown a red card for defending himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Derby_Incident_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Derby_Incident-18">[18]</a></sup> In the aftermath of the event, both teams had 1 point redacted and forfeited the match. However, this event didn't stop Maccabi Tel Aviv from being the first Israeli Team to win all three local Trophies: the <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Premier_League" title="Israeli Premier League">Israeli Premier League</a> the <a href="/wiki/Israel_State_Cup" title="Israel State Cup">Israel State Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Toto_Cup" title="Toto Cup">Toto Cup</a>. Notable new players in the team were <a href="/wiki/Nosa_Igiebor" title="Nosa Igiebor">Nosa Igiebor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eden_Ben_Basat" title="Eden Ben Basat">Eden Ben Basat</a>. The best player in the squad was still <a href="/wiki/Eran_Zahavi" title="Eran Zahavi">Eran Zahavi</a> who broke the Israeli Record for consecutive scoring games and scored 27 goals throughout the season.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shota_Arveladze.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="700" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Shota_Arveladze.jpg/200px-Shota_Arveladze.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Shota_Arveladze.jpg/300px-Shota_Arveladze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Shota_Arveladze.jpg/400px-Shota_Arveladze.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shota_Arveladze.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Shota_Arveladze" title="Shota Arveladze">Shota Arveladze</a>, Current Head Coach</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 2015–16 season, the team qualified for the UEFA Champions League group stage for the first time in 11 years. They were a member of Group G, along with <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Group_G_14.2F15_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Group_G_14.2F15-19">[19]</a></sup> However, these three elite clubs proved to be too much for Maccabi Tel Aviv to handle, and they lost all 6 of their group stage matches, scoring just 1 goal while conceding 16. In the league, Maccabi's main rivals for the title were <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Be%27er_Sheva_F.C." title="Hapoel Be'er Sheva F.C.">Hapoel Be'er Sheva</a>. After a loss to Hapoel Be'er Sheva at <a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_Stadium" title="Bloomfield Stadium">Bloomfield Stadium</a> thanks to two clinical touches from <a href="/wiki/Elyaniv_Barda" title="Elyaniv Barda">Elyaniv Barda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maor_Melikson" title="Maor Melikson">Maor Melikson</a>, head coach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavisa_Jokanovic" title="Slavisa Jokanovic">Slavisa Jokanovic</a> was signed by <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> and he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Bosz" title="Peter Bosz">Peter Bosz</a>, who helped improve Maccabi's performances in the league. Be'er Sheva fell under huge pressure before the end of the season, which helped Maccabi fight back and get into the title race again. Maccabi managed to take advantage of Be'er Sheva's bad results, beating <a href="/wiki/Beitar_Jerusalem_F.C." title="Beitar Jerusalem F.C.">Beitar Jerusalem</a> in a close and dramatic tie, where <a href="/wiki/Eran_Zahavi" title="Eran Zahavi">Eran Zahavi</a> scored the winning goal for Maccabi in the 90th minute, breaking the goalscoring record of <a href="/wiki/Nisim_Elmaliah" title="Nisim Elmaliah">Nisim Elmaliah</a> by scoring more than 31 goals in one league season. In the biggest game of the season, against Hapoel Be'er Sheva, a win would have brought Maccabi to 1st place because of their goal difference, while any other result would have left Hapoel Be'er Sheva alone at 1st place with a 3 points advantage and only 3 games to go. Maccabi tied the game 0-0, leaving Hapoel Be'er Sheva 3 points ahead of Maccabi and top of the league. Maccabi continued their bad form and dropped points again in their next game, this time against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hapoel_Ra%27anana_F.C." title="Hapoel Ra'anana F.C.">Hapoel Ra'anana</a>, drawing 1-1, and the title came closer to Hapoel Be'er Sheva, who had a 5 points advantage with only 2 games to go. The last game of the league season was a rollercoaster of emotions for Maccabi fans who were hoping for Be'er Sheva to lose against Sakhnin, and who needed to defeat Maccabi Haifa to win the championship. Sakhnin took the lead after 6 minutes, however Be'er Sheva responded quickly and got a goal after only 10 minutes. At that stage, Be'er Sheva were champions as Maccabi kept on searching for a goal, which finally came when Eran Zahavi scored, which meant Maccabi were the champions at the time. 12 minutes after Maccabi's goal, Be'er Sheva went 2-1 up. Maccabi got a 6-0 lead over Haifa, but were unable to win the title, as Be'er Sheva had scored a third goal and became champions. The cup final was Maccabi's last chance to win a trophy this season, and they faced Maccabi Haifa in the final. However, Haifa defeated Maccabi and won their first cup in 18 years, which caused Peter Bosz to go to Ajax as Maccabi had finished with no trophies. The 2015-16 season was called "the worst year in Jordi's Era". To make things worse, Eran Zahavi, the star player of Maccabi, was sold to <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_R%26F_F.C." title="Guangzhou R&amp;F F.C.">Guangzhou R&amp;F</a> for 8.5 million dollars at the end of the season.</p>
<p>Before the beginning of the 2016-17 season, Maccabi hired <a href="/wiki/Shota_Arveladze" title="Shota Arveladze">Shota Arveladze</a> as their new coach and signed several new players such as <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B0ar_%C3%96rn_Kjartansson" title="Viðar Örn Kjartansson">Viðar Örn Kjartansson</a> from <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6_FF" title="Malmö FF">Malmö FF</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yossi_Benayoun" title="Yossi Benayoun">Yossi Benayoun</a> from <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Haifa_F.C." title="Maccabi Haifa F.C.">Maccabi Haifa</a>. They started the season well, defeating <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Hapoel Tel Aviv F.C.">Hapoel Tel Aviv</a> 5-0 on 25 September 2016, with goals from <a href="/wiki/Nosa_Igiebor" title="Nosa Igiebor">Nosa Igiebor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tal_Ben_Haim_(footballer,_born_1989)" title="Tal Ben Haim (footballer, born 1989)">Tal Ben Haim</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vi%C3%B0ar_%C3%96rn_Kjartansson" title="Viðar Örn Kjartansson">Viðar Örn Kjartansson</a> for their biggest win in the <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv_derby" title="Tel Aviv derby">Tel Aviv derby</a> game since 1970.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters_and_rivals">Supporters and rivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Supporters and rivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Maccabi has one main fan organization, "Maccabi Fanatics" . they are located in Gate 11. Maccabi Fanatics as an organization involves in many ways. Maccabi Fanatics are close friends with <a href="/wiki/VAK410" title="VAK410">VAK410</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afc_ajax" title="Afc ajax">Ajax</a> ultras) since the 2000s.</p>
<p>Maccabi's main rivals are <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Hapoel Tel Aviv F.C.">Hapoel Tel Aviv</a>. The matches between the teams gain a lot of attention in the Israeli public and are referred to as the "Big <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv_derby" title="Tel Aviv derby">Tel Aviv derby</a>" (as opposed to the "Small Tel Aviv derby", matches between <a href="/wiki/Bnei_Yehuda_Tel_Aviv_F.C." title="Bnei Yehuda Tel Aviv F.C.">Bnei Yehuda</a> and Maccabi or Hapoel). Other rivalries include, to a lesser extent, those with <a href="/wiki/Beitar_Jerusalem_F.C." title="Beitar Jerusalem F.C.">Beitar Jerusalem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hapoel_Be%27er_Sheva_F.C." title="Hapoel Be'er Sheva F.C.">Hapoel Be'er Sheva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Haifa_F.C." title="Maccabi Haifa F.C.">Maccabi Haifa</a>.</p>
<p>A survey conducted in March 2012 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yedioth" title="Yedioth">Yedioth</a> showed that Maccabi Tel Aviv was the second most popular team among Israeli football fans (23%). Same survey revealed that 33% of Tel Aviv residents support the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium_and_Training_Ground">Stadium and Training Ground</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Stadium and Training Ground">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maccabiah_Stadium" title="Maccabiah Stadium">Maccabiah Stadium</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ramat_Gan_Stadium" title="Ramat Gan Stadium">Ramat Gan Stadium</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_Stadium" title="Bloomfield Stadium">Bloomfield Stadium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg/250px-Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg/375px-Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg/500px-Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bloomfield_Stadium21.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_Stadium" title="Bloomfield Stadium">Bloomfield Stadium</a> of Jaffa. Maccabi's home ground</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_Stadium" title="Bloomfield Stadium">Bloomfield Stadium</a> in Tel Aviv Yafo is Maccabi Tel Aviv's home ground and seats approximately 14,413 fans. The Stadium has been recently upgraded to allow the spectators to enjoy improved seating and a better game experience.</p>
<p>The Maccabi Tel Aviv Training Ground is located in south Tel Aviv, near the <a href="/wiki/Holon" title="Holon">Holon</a> Intersection and on the outskirts of the <a href="/wiki/Kiryat_Shalom" title="Kiryat Shalom">Kiryat Shalom</a> neighbourhood. The various Maccabi Tel Aviv teams began practicing at the complex in the mid 1970s, starting with the Youth Division teams, and joined later by the senior team. The facility consists of four pitches that serve all the Maccabi Tel Aviv teams and includes two gyms, treatment rooms and classrooms. The senior team practice at the western facility, near the locker rooms, on an area one and a half times larger than a regular football pitch, with renovated terraces that seat approximately 100 fans.</p>
<p>On 6 March 2012, the Youth Division Complex was officially re-dedicated in the name of the late <a href="/wiki/Avi_Cohen" title="Avi Cohen">Avi Cohen</a>.</p>
<p>Not far from the senior team's training ground is a synthetic pitch, one of the first of its kind in Israel, which serves as the training ground for all the teams in the Maccabi Tel Aviv Youth Division. At the northern end of the complex is the central pitch of the Youth Division, lined by two terraces with a seating capacity of over 200 and equipped for television broadcasts. The central pitch is used primarily by the Maccabi Tel Aviv Under-19 squad, but the club's youth teams also make use of the facility. The fourth and smallest of the pitches is the eastern one, used mainly for training and frequently for matches of the children's teams. The Youth Division complex has ten dressing rooms, one of which is used by visiting teams and one extra room for the referees on match days. During the 2011–12 season an exercise room was also built on the ground for the use of the entire Youth Division.</p>
<p>Ever since 2015, <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Ofer_Stadium" title="Sammy Ofer Stadium">Sammy Ofer Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a> is being used as the home stadium of Maccabi Tel Aviv for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> group stage. It is considered to be a world-class standard stadium. This stadium also hosts matches of the <a href="/wiki/Israel_national_football_team" title="Israel national football team">Israel national football team</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Maccabi_Tel_Aviv_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li><b>12</b> <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel"><img alt="Israel" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="660" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" width="21"/></a></span> – <a href="/wiki/Meni_Levi" title="Meni Levi">Meni Levi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defender_(football)" title="Defender (football)">Right back</a></li>
</ul>
